TI Entrepreneurial intervention in an electronic market place
SO DEVELOPMENTS IN APPLIED ARTIFICAIL INTELLIGENCE, PROCEEDINGS
SE LECTURE NOTES IN ARTIFICIAL INTELLIGENCE
LA English
DT Article; Proceedings Paper
CT 15th International Conference on Industrial and Engineering Applications
   of Artificial Intelligence and Expert Systems (IEA/AIE 2002)
CY JUN, 2002
CL CAIRNS, AUSTRALIA
SP Int Soc Appl Intelligence
ID AGENTS
AB An electronic market has been constructed in an on-going collaborative research project between a university and a software house. The way in which actors (buyers, sellers and others) use the market will be influenced by the information available to them, including information drawn from outside the immediate market environment. In this experiment, data mining and filtering techniques are used to distil both individual signals drawn from the markets and signals from the Internet into meaningful advice for the actors. The goal of this experiment is first to learn how actors will use the advice available to them, and second how the market will evolve through entrepreneurial intervention. In this electronic market a multiagent process management system is used to manage all market transactions including those that drive the market evolutionary process.

TI Gikomba market literature: Reflections on the identity and aspirations
   of a common entrepreneurial folk
SO FABULA
LA English
DT Article; Proceedings Paper
CT Conference of the International-Society-for-Folk-Narrative Research
   (ISFNR)
CY JUL 11-17, 2000
CL NAIROBI, KENYA
SP Int Soc Folk Narrat Res
AB Literary creativity, it would appear, is closely linked to humankind's cognitive and psycholinguistic make-up. Far from the traditional meaning of the term 'literary' - which implies the written medium - this creativity will be found in all human groups. The creative forms that emerge from a discourse group are indeed reflections of the identity of the group; its aspirations, its worldview and its relationship with the other social forces and groups are echoed in the literary pieces that are churned by its members. The research in question was proposed against the background just outlined. Participant observation was mainly used in the 're-construction' and collection of the literary pieces analyzed. Gikomba Market Literature, it was discovered, has its distinct form and character. The narrative mode engenders the audience to fully participate in the unravelling of a story inserting fillers and asides which themselves reflect on the urgency and social context in which participants daily engage. Together with their audience, story-tellers will jump back and forth in time and geographical space to enrich their narration, falsely cut story-lines to sell a thing or two... and then move on... Such poetic license has the effect of contextualising the narration, and making it part of real life. Gikomba oral narrative clearly outline the entrepreneurs as a social group. The group, which is open to jobless school leavers and drop-outs, struggles to make ends meet: initially to have a reasonable income, and later to climb high up the social ladder. Indeed some have aspired successfully to political office, and, according to various narratives, such folk have turned their faces away from the plight of their former companions.

TI Strategies for service and market development of entrepreneurial
   software designing firms
SO TECHNOVATION
LA English
DT Article
DE technology-based entrepreneurship; business strategy; technology
   strategy; technological capability; software development
ID TECHNOLOGY-BASED FIRMS; HIGH-TECH FIRMS; INNOVATION; CORPORATE;
   PERFORMANCE; NETWORKS
AB Based on a review of the literature of new technology-based firms, this study developed a strategic management framework for service and market development of entrepreneurial software firms (ESFs) by integrating business with technology strategies. Testing the strategic management framework in a pilot sample in Malaysia showed that vulnerability, market uncertainty, rapid technological change and development, and lack of resources, especially human resources, were constraining the growth and development of these software firms. The study found that for their product development, the Malaysian ESFs lacked a clear strategic focus on developing technological superiority, and accessing multiple sources of technology. Strategies critical for software market develop ment that need to be improved were the speed to market entry, linkage with large customers, and development of appropriate distribution channels. Long term policy, top management commitment, responsiveness to change, and creation of an innovation accepting. entrepreneurship accommodating culture were found to be important facilitators for innovating new software. (C) 2001 Elsevier Science Ltd. All rights reserved.
